window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Foo_Fighters';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"fighters,_,foo,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p>The
<b>Foo
Fighters</b>
are
an
American
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
music">rock</a>
band,
formed
in
<a
href="/wiki/Seattle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Seattle">Seattle</a>
in
1994.
It
was
founded
by
<a
href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nirvana
(band)">Nirvana</a>
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Dave_Grohl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave
Grohl">Dave
Grohl</a>
as
a
one-man
project
following
the
death
of
<a
href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kurt
Cobain">Kurt
Cobain</a>
and
the
resulting
dissolution
of
his
previous
band.
The
group
got
its
name
from
the
<a
href="/wiki/Unidentified_flying_object?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Unidentified
flying
object">UFOs</a>
and
various
aerial
phenomena
that
were
reported
by
<a
href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Allies
of
World
War
II">Allied
aircraft
pilots</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/World_War_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="World
War
II">World
War
II</a>,
which
were
known
collectively
as
<a
href="/wiki/Foo_fighter?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Foo
fighter">foo
fighters</a>.
Prior
to
the
release
of
Foo
Fighters'
1995
debut
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Foo
Fighters
(album)">Foo
Fighters</a></i>,
which
featured
Grohl
as
the
only
official
member,
Grohl
recruited
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Nate_Mendel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nate
Mendel">Nate
Mendel</a>
and
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/William_Goldsmith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="William
Goldsmith">William
Goldsmith</a>,
both
formerly
of
<a
href="/wiki/Sunny_Day_Real_Estate?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sunny
Day
Real
Estate">Sunny
Day
Real
Estate</a>,
as
well
as
fellow
Nirvana
touring
bandmate
<a
href="/wiki/Pat_Smear?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pat
Smear">Pat
Smear</a>
as
guitarist
to
complete
the
lineup.
The
band
began
with
performances
in
<a
href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Portland,
Oregon">Portland,
Oregon</a>.
Goldsmith
quit
during
the
recording
of
the
group's
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Colour_and_the_Shape?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Colour
and
the
Shape">The
Colour
and
the
Shape</a></i>
(1997)
when
most
of
the
drum
parts
were
re-recorded
by
Grohl
himself.
Smear's
departure
followed
soon
afterward.</p>








<p>They
were
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Taylor_Hawkins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Taylor
Hawkins">Taylor
Hawkins</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Franz_Stahl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Franz
Stahl">Franz
Stahl</a>,
respectively,
although
Stahl
was
fired
before
the
recording
of
the
group's
third
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/There_Is_Nothing_Left_to_Lose?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="There
Is
Nothing
Left
to
Lose">There
Is
Nothing
Left
to
Lose</a></i>
(1999).
The
band
briefly
continued
as
a
trio
until
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Shiflett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Shiflett">Chris
Shiflett</a>
joined
as
the
band's
lead
guitarist
after
the
completion
of
<i>There
Is
Nothing
Left
to
Lose</i>.
The
band
released
its
fourth
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/One_by_One_(Foo_Fighters_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
by
One
(Foo
Fighters
album)">One
by
One</a></i>,
in
2002.
The
group
followed
that
release
with
the
two-disc
<i><a
href="/wiki/In_Your_Honor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Your
Honor">In
Your
Honor</a></i>
(2005),
which
was
split
between
<a
href="/wiki/Acoustic_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Acoustic
music">acoustic</a>
songs
and
heavier
material.
Foo
Fighters
released
its
sixth
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Echoes,_Silence,_Patience_%26_Grace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace">Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace</a></i>,
in
2007.
In
2010,
it
was
confirmed
that
Smear
had
officially
rejoined
the
band
after
touring
with
Foo
Fighters
as
an
unofficial
member
between
2006
and
2009.
Over
the
course
of
the
band's
career,
four
of
its
albums
have
won
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Album">Best
Rock
Album</a>.
The
band's
seventh
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wasting_Light?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wasting
Light">Wasting
Light</a></i>,
was
released
in
2011.
Grohl
stated
in
January
2013
that
the
band
had
started
writing
material
for
an
eighth
studio
album.
Producer
<a
href="/wiki/Butch_Vig?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Butch
Vig">Butch
Vig</a>
is
set
to
produce
his
second
album
with
the
group.</p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="History">History</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
History">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Formation_and_debut_album_.281994.E2.80.931995.29">Formation
and
debut
album
(1994–1995)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Formation
and
debut
album
(1994–1995)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:172px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dave_Grohl_in_London.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dave_Grohl_in_London.jpg/170px-Dave_Grohl_in_London.jpg"
width="170"
height="226"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dave_Grohl_in_London.jpg/255px-Dave_Grohl_in_London.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dave_Grohl_in_London.jpg/340px-Dave_Grohl_in_London.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dave_Grohl_in_London.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>











<a
href="/wiki/Dave_Grohl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave
Grohl">Dave
Grohl</a>
(pictured
in
2006)
founded
Foo
Fighters
after
his
previous
band











<a
href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nirvana
(band)">Nirvana</a>
broke
up
in
1994.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Grohl
joined
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grunge?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grunge">grunge</a>
group
<a
href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nirvana
(band)">Nirvana</a>
as
its
drummer
in
1990.
During
tours,
he
took
a
guitar
with
him
and
wrote
songs.
Grohl
held
back
these
songs
from
the
rest
of
the
band;
he
said
in
1997,
&quot;I
was
in
awe
of
[frontman
<a
href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kurt
Cobain">Kurt
Cobain</a>'s
songs],
and
[I
was]
intimidated.
I
thought
it
was
best
that
I
kept
my
songs
to
myself.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Foobulous_4-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Foobulous-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Grohl
occasionally
booked
studio
time
to
record
demos
and
covers
of
songs
he
liked
and
even
issued
a
cassette
of
some
of
those
songs
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pocketwatch_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pocketwatch
(album)">Pocketwatch</a></i>
under
the
pseudonym
&quot;Late!&quot;
in
1992.<sup
id="cite_ref-Alien_parking_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Alien_parking-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Frontman
<a
href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kurt
Cobain">Kurt
Cobain</a>
was
found
dead
in
his
Seattle
home
on
April
8,
1994,
and
Nirvana
subsequently
disbanded.
Grohl
received
offers
to
work
with
various
artists;
he
almost
accepted
a
permanent
position
as
drummer
in
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Petty_and_the_Heartbreakers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Petty
and
the
Heartbreakers">Tom
Petty
and
the
Heartbreakers</a>.
Ultimately
Grohl
declined
and
instead
entered
<a
href="/wiki/Robert_Lang_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Robert
Lang
Studios">Robert
Lang
Studios</a>
in
October
1994
to
record
fifteen
of
the
forty
songs
he
had
written.<sup
id="cite_ref-Alien_parking_5-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Alien_parking-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
With
the
exception
of
a
guitar
part
on
&quot;X-Static&quot;,
played
by
<a
href="/wiki/Greg_Dulli?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greg
Dulli">Greg
Dulli</a>
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Afghan_Whigs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Afghan
Whigs"
class="mw-redirect">Afghan
Whigs</a>,
Dave
Grohl
played
every
instrument
and
sang
every
vocal
on
the
tracks.<sup
id="cite_ref-AMG_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMG-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;I
was
supposed
to
just
join
another
band
and
be
a
drummer
the
rest
of
my
life,&quot;
Grohl
later
said.
&quot;I
thought
that
I
would
rather
do
what
no
one
expected
me
to
do.
I
enjoy
writing
music
and
I
enjoy
trying
to
sing,
and
there's
nothing
anyone
can
really
do
to
discourage
me.&quot;
Grohl
completed
an
album's
worth
of
material
in
five
days
and
handed
out
cassette
copies
of
the
sessions
to
his
friends
for
feedback.<sup
id="cite_ref-Alien_parking_5-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Alien_parking-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Grohl
hoped
to
keep
his
anonymity
and
release
the
recordings
in
a
limited
run
under
the
title
&quot;Foo
Fighters&quot;,
taken
from
the
<a
href="/wiki/World_War_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="World
War
II">World
War
II</a>
term
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Foo_fighter?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Foo
fighter">foo
fighter</a>&quot;,
used
to
refer
to
<a
href="/wiki/Unidentified_flying_object?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Unidentified
flying
object">unidentified
flying
objects</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Alien_parking_5-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Alien_parking-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
the
demo
tape
circulated
in
the
music
industry,
creating
interest
among
record
labels.<sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
Grohl
formed
a
band
to
support
the
album.
Initially,
he
talked
to
former
Nirvana
band
mate
<a
href="/wiki/Krist_Novoselic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Krist
Novoselic">Krist
Novoselic</a>
about
joining
the
group,
but
both
decided
against
it.
&quot;For
Krist
and
I,
it
would
have
felt
really
natural
and
really
great&quot;,
Grohl
explained.
&quot;But
for
everyone
else,
it
would
have
been
weird,
and
it
would
have
left
me
in
a
really
bad
position.
Then
I
really
would
have
been
under
the
microscope.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Having
heard
about
the
disbanding
of
<a
href="/wiki/Seattle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Seattle">Seattle</a>-based
rock
band
<a
href="/wiki/Sunny_Day_Real_Estate?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sunny
Day
Real
Estate">Sunny
Day
Real
Estate</a>,
Grohl
drafted
the
group's
bass
player,
<a
href="/wiki/Nate_Mendel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nate
Mendel">Nate
Mendel</a>,
and
drummer,
<a
href="/wiki/William_Goldsmith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="William
Goldsmith">William
Goldsmith</a>.
Grohl
asked
<a
href="/wiki/Pat_Smear?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pat
Smear">Pat
Smear</a>,
who
served
as
a
touring
guitarist
for
Nirvana
after
the
release
of
its
1993
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/In_Utero_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Utero
(album)">In
Utero</a></i>,
to
join
as
the
group's
second
guitarist.<sup
id="cite_ref-Breakout_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Breakout-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
Grohl
ultimately
licensed
the
album
to
<a
href="/wiki/Capitol_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Capitol
Records">Capitol
Records</a>,
releasing
it
on
his
new
record
label,
Roswell
Records.<sup
id="cite_ref-Alien_parking_5-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Alien_parking-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Foo
Fighters
made
its
live
public
debut
on
February
23,
1995
at
the
Jambalaya
Club
in
Arcata,
California
and
then
March
3
at
<a
href="/wiki/Satyricon_nightclub?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Satyricon
nightclub"
class="mw-redirect">The
Satyricon</a>
in
Portland.
They
followed
that
with
a
show
at
the
Velvet
Elvis
in
Seattle
on
March
4.
The
March
3
show
had
been
part
of
a
benefit
gig
to
aid
the
finances
of
the
investigation
into
the
rape
and
murder
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Gits?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Gits">The
Gits</a>
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Mia_Zapata?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mia
Zapata">Mia
Zapata</a>.
Grohl
refused
to
do
interviews
or
tour
large
venues
to
promote
the
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-Breakout_9-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Breakout-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
Foo
Fighters
undertook
its
first
major
tour
in
the
spring
of
1995,
opening
for
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Watt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Watt">Mike
Watt</a>.
The
band's
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Is_a_Call?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="This
Is
a
Call">This
Is
a
Call</a>&quot;,
was
released
in
June
1995,<sup
id="cite_ref-AMG_6-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMG-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
its
debut
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Foo
Fighters
(album)">Foo
Fighters</a></i>
was
released
the
next
month.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I%27ll_Stick_Around?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I'll
Stick
Around">I'll
Stick
Around</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/For_All_the_Cows?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="For
All
the
Cows">For
All
the
Cows</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Big_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
Me">Big
Me</a>&quot;
were
released
as
subsequent
singles.
The
band
spent
the
following
months
on
tour,
including
their
first
appearance
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Reading_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reading
Festival"
class="mw-redirect">Reading
Festival</a>
in
England
in
August.<sup
id="cite_ref-Breakout_9-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Breakout-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="The_Colour_and_the_Shape_.281996.E2.80.931997.29"><i>The
Colour
and
the
Shape</i>
(1996–1997)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
The
Colour
and
the
Shape
(1996–1997)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>After
touring
through
the
spring
of
1996,
Foo
Fighters
entered
Bear
Creek
Studio
in
<a
href="/wiki/Woodinville,_Washington?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Woodinville,
Washington">Woodinville,
Washington</a>
with
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Gil_Norton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gil
Norton">Gil
Norton</a>
to
record
its
second
album.
While
Grohl
once
again
wrote
all
the
songs,
the
rest
of
the
band
collaborated
on
the
arrangements.
With
the
sessions
nearly
complete,
Grohl
took
the
rough
mixes
with
him
to
Los
Angeles,
intending
to
finish
up
his
vocal
and
guitar
parts.
While
there,
Grohl
realized
that
he
was
not
happy
with
how
the
mixes
were
turning
out,
and
the
band
&quot;basically
re-recorded
almost
everything&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Foobulous_4-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Foobulous-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
L.A.
sessions,
Grohl
had
played
drums
on
the
songs.
Unhappy
with
Goldsmith's
drumming,
Grohl
removed
it
from
the
recordings
and
re-recorded
the
drum
tracks.
As
Goldsmith
was
about
to
come
down
to
L.A.
to
find
out
why
he
wasn't
being
called
upon
to
re-record
his
parts,
he
called
Mendel
from
Seattle
inquiring
if
he
should
make
the
trip.
Grohl
then
called
Goldsmith
saying,
&quot;Dude,
don't
come
down
here,
I'm
recording
some
of
the
drum
tracks.&quot;
Shocked
by
this,
Goldsmith
met
up
with
Mendel
in
Seattle
and
repeated
Grohl's
claim
to
be
re-recording
&quot;some&quot;
of
the
tracks.
Mendel
asked,
&quot;Is
that
what
he
told
you?&quot;
Goldsmith
affirmed
it,
and
Mendel
stated,
&quot;No,
man
--
he
did
them
all.&quot;</p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:TaylorHawkins.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/TaylorHawkins.jpg/220px-TaylorHawkins.jpg"
width="220"
height="165"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/TaylorHawkins.jpg/330px-TaylorHawkins.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/TaylorHawkins.jpg/440px-TaylorHawkins.jpg
2x"
/></a>

class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a

/></a>










</div>
Long-time
drummer











<a
href="/wiki/Taylor_Hawkins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Taylor
Hawkins">Taylor
Hawkins</a>
(pictured
in
2012)
joined
the
band
in
1997.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Grohl
explained
that
he'd
wanted
the
drums
to
sound
a
certain
way
on
the
album.
He
wanted
Goldsmith
to
play
for
the
tour
even
though
it
would
not
be
his
drumming
but
Grohl's
on
the
album.
Feeling
betrayed,
Goldsmith
left
the
band.
To
this
day
Grohl
still
feels
guilty
for
his
decision,
saying
&quot;I
was
an
immature
kid
at
the
time.&quot;
However,
he
felt
that
he
did
what
he
had
to
do
to
give
the
record
the
right
sound
and
make
it
successful.<sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
need
of
a
replacement
for
Goldsmith,
Grohl
contacted
<a
href="/wiki/Alanis_Morissette?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alanis
Morissette">Alanis
Morissette</a>'s
touring
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Taylor_Hawkins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Taylor
Hawkins">Taylor
Hawkins</a>
to
see
if
he
could
recommend
anybody.
Grohl
was
surprised
when
Hawkins
volunteered
his
own
services
as
drummer.<sup
id="cite_ref-Foobulous_4-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Foobulous-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Hawkins
made
his
debut
with
the
group
in
time
for
the
release
of
its
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Colour_and_the_Shape?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Colour
and
the
Shape">The
Colour
and
the
Shape</a></i>,
in
May
1997.
The
album
included
the
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Monkey_Wrench_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monkey
Wrench
(song)">Monkey
Wrench</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/My_Hero_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="My
Hero
(song)">My
Hero</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Everlong?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Everlong">Everlong</a>&quot;.</p>








<p>Pat
Smear
announced
to
the
rest
of
the
group
that
he
wanted
to
leave
the
band
claiming
exhaustion
and
burnout
but
agreed
to
stay
with
the
band
until
a
replacement
could
be
found
for
him.
Four
months
later
in
September
1997
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award">MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>,
Smear
simultaneously
announced
to
the
public
his
departure
from
the
band
and
introduced
his
replacement,
Grohl's
former
<a
href="/wiki/Scream_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scream
(band)">Scream</a>
bandmate
<a
href="/wiki/Franz_Stahl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Franz
Stahl">Franz
Stahl</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Kerrang_1997_11-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Kerrang_1997-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
Stahl
toured
with
the
band
for
the
next
few
months,
and
appeared
on
two
tracks
that
the
band
recorded
for
movie
soundtracks,
a
re-recording
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Walking_After_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walking
After
You">Walking
After
You</a>&quot;
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_X-Files_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
X-Files
(film)">The
X-Files</a></i>
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/A320_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A320
(song)"
class="mw-redirect">A320</a>&quot;
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/Godzilla_(1998_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Godzilla
(1998
film)">Godzilla</a></i>.
A
B-side
of
the
album,
&quot;Dear
Lover&quot;,
appeared
in
the
horror
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Scream_2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scream
2">Scream
2</a></i>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="There_Is_Nothing_Left_to_Lose_.281998.E2.80.932001.29"><i>There
Is
Nothing
Left
to
Lose</i>
(1998–2001)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
There
Is
Nothing
Left
to
Lose
(1998–2001)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1998,
Foo
Fighters
traveled
to
Grohl's
home
state
of
Virginia
to
write
music
for
its
third
album.
However,
Grohl
and
Stahl
were
unable
to
co-operate
as
songwriters;
Grohl
told
<i><a
href="/wiki/Kerrang!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kerrang!">Kerrang!</a></i>
in
1999,
&quot;in
those
few
weeks
it
just
seemed
like
the
three
of
us
were
moving
in
one
direction
and
Franz
wasn't&quot;.
Grohl
was
distraught
over
the
decision
to
fire
Stahl,
as
the
two
had
been
friends
since
childhood.
Shortly
after
that,
Mendel
called
Grohl
to
say
he
was
quitting
the
band
to
reunite
with
Sunny
Day
Real
Estate,
only
to
reverse
his
decision
the
next
day.<sup
id="cite_ref-Burn_away_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Burn_away-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
remaining
trio
of
Grohl,
Mendel,
and
Hawkins
spent
the
next
several
months
recording
the
band's
third
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/There_Is_Nothing_Left_to_Lose?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="There
Is
Nothing
Left
to
Lose">There
Is
Nothing
Left
to
Lose</a></i>,
in
Grohl's
Virginia
home
studio
that
he
bought
and
built.
The
album
spawned
several
singles,
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Learn_to_Fly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Learn
to
Fly">Learn
to
Fly</a>&quot;,
the
band's
first
single
to
reach
the
US
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100</a>.</p>








<p>Before
the
release
of
the
album,
Capitol
president
Gary
Gersh
was
forced
out
of
the
label.
Given
Grohl's
history
with
Gersh,
Foo
Fighters'
contract
had
included
a
&quot;key
man
clause&quot;
that
allowed
them
to
leave
the
label
upon
Gersh's
departure.
They
subsequently
left
Capitol
and
signed
with
<a
href="/wiki/RCA_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RCA
Records">RCA</a>,
who
later
acquired
the
rights
to
the
band's
Capitol
albums.<sup
id="cite_ref-Burn_away_12-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Burn_away-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
recording
for
<i>There
Is
Nothing
Left
to
Lose</i>
was
completed,
the
band
auditioned
a
number
of
potential
guitarists,
and
eventually
settled
on
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Shiflett?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Shiflett">Chris
Shiflett</a>,
who
performs
with
<a
href="/wiki/Me_First_and_the_Gimme_Gimmes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Me
First
and
the
Gimme
Gimmes">Me
First
and
the
Gimme
Gimmes</a>,
and
previously
performed
with
California
punk
band,
<a
href="/wiki/No_Use_for_a_Name?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="No
Use
for
a
Name">No
Use
for
a
Name</a>.
Shiflett
initially
joined
the
band
as
touring
guitarist,
but
achieved
full-time
status
prior
to
the
recording
of
the
group's
fourth
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-back_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-back-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Around
2001,
Foo
Fighters
established
a
relationship
with
rock
band
<a
href="/wiki/Queen_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Queen
(band)">Queen</a>,
of
whom
the
band
(particularly
Grohl<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
Hawkins<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>)
were
fans.
In
March
of
that
year,
Grohl
and
Hawkins
inducted
the
band
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_%26_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
&amp;
Roll
Hall
of
Fame"
class="mw-redirect">Rock
&amp;
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a><sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
joined
them
on
stage
for
a
rendition
of
the
Queen
1976
classic
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tie_Your_Mother_Down?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tie
Your
Mother
Down">Tie
Your
Mother
Down</a>&quot;,
with
Hawkins
playing
drums
alongside
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Meddows-Taylor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Meddows-Taylor"
class="mw-redirect">Roger
Taylor</a>,
while
Grohl
was
playing
rhythm
guitar
and
handling
vocal
duties.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
Guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Brian_May?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brian
May">Brian
May</a>
added
a
guitar
track
to
Foo
Fighters'
second
cover
of
<a
href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pink
Floyd">Pink
Floyd</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Have_a_Cigar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Have
a
Cigar">Have
a
Cigar</a>&quot;,
which
appeared
on
the
soundtrack
to
the
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mission:_Impossible_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mission:
Impossible
II">Mission:
Impossible
II</a></i>.
In
2002,
guitarist
May
contributed
guitar
work
to
&quot;Tired
of
You&quot;
and
an
outtake
called
&quot;Knucklehead&quot;.
The
bands
have
performed
together
on
several
occasions
since,
including
<a
href="/wiki/VH1_Rock_Honors?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1
Rock
Honors">VH1
Rock
Honors</a>
and
Foo
Fighters'
headlining
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hyde
Park,
London">Hyde
Park</a>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="One_by_One_.282001.E2.80.932004.29"><i>One
by
One</i>
(2001–2004)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
One
by
One
(2001–2004)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Near
the
end
of
2001,
the
band
reconvened
to
record
its
<a
href="/wiki/One_by_One_(Foo_Fighters_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
by
One
(Foo
Fighters
album)">fourth
album</a>.
After
spending
four
months
in
a
Los
Angeles
studio
completing
the
album,
the
album
&quot;just
didn't
sound
right&quot;
and
the
band
had
no
confidence
in
the
album
to
sell
many
records.
With
the
album
not
reaching
their
expectations,
and
much
infighting
amongst
the
members,
Grohl
spent
some
time
helping
<a
href="/wiki/Queens_of_the_Stone_Age?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Queens
of
the
Stone
Age">Queens
of
the
Stone
Age</a>
complete
their
2002
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Songs_for_the_Deaf?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Songs
for
the
Deaf">Songs
for
the
Deaf</a></i>.
Once
the
Queens
of
the
Stone
Age
album
was
finished,
and
touring
had
started
for
both
Foo
Fighters
and
Queens
of
the
Stone
Age,
the
band
was
on
the
verge
of
breaking
up
entirely
as
the
animosity
grew
amongst
the
members.
Grohl
reconvened
with
Hawkins,
Shiflett
and
Mendel
to
have
them
play
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coachella
Valley
Music
and
Arts
Festival">Coachella
Festival</a>,
with
Queens
of
the
Stone
Age
playing
one
day
and
Foo
Fighters
the
following.
After
the
Queens
of
the
Stone
Age
played,
Hawkins
and
Grohl
talked
about
retrying
the
<i>One
by
One</i>
album
and
had
agreed
to
finishing
it
and
seeing
where
they
would
go
from
there.
The
group
went
and
re-recorded
nearly
all
of
the
album
(save
&quot;Tired
of
You&quot;)
in
a
ten-day
stretch
at
Grohl's
home
studio
in
Alexandria,
<a
href="/wiki/Virginia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Virginia">Virginia</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-back_13-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-back-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
original
version
of
<i>One
by
One</i>,
referred
by
the
band
as
&quot;Million
Dollar
Demos&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-spin_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-spin-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
has
never
been
heard
in
its
entirety,
except
for
snippets
which
leaked
before
the
album's
premiere,
and
a
few
more
snippets
leaked
by
a
fan
on
the
band's
website
in
2007.
Two
songs
from
these
sessions
were
leaked
in
2012.</p>








<p>The
final
album
was
released
in
October
2002
under
the
title
<i><a
href="/wiki/One_by_One_(Foo_Fighters_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
by
One
(Foo
Fighters
album)">One
by
One</a></i>.
Singles
from
the
album
included
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/All_My_Life_(Foo_Fighters_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
My
Life
(Foo
Fighters
song)">All
My
Life</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Times_Like_These_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Times
Like
These
(song)">Times
Like
These</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Low_(Foo_Fighters_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Low
(Foo
Fighters
song)">Low</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Have_It_All_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Have
It
All
(song)">Have
It
All</a>&quot;.</p>








<p>For
most
of
its
history,
the
band
chose
to
stay
away
from
the
political
realm.
However,
in
2004,
upon
learning
that
<a
href="/wiki/George_W._Bush?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
W.
Bush">George
W.
Bush</a>'s
presidential
campaign
was
using
&quot;Times
Like
These&quot;
at
rallies,
Grohl
decided
to
lend
his
public
support
to
<a
href="/wiki/John_Kerry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Kerry">John
Kerry</a>'s
campaign
-
&quot;There’s
no
way
of
stopping
the
president
playing
your
songs,
so
I
went
out
and
played
it
for
John
Kerry’s
people
instead,
where
I
thought
the
message
would
kinda
make
more
sense&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-xfm_19-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-xfm-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
Grohl
attended
several
Kerry
rallies
and
occasionally
performed
solo
acoustic
sets.
The
entire
band
eventually
joined
Grohl
for
a
performance
in
Arizona
coinciding
with
one
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election_debates?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U.S.
presidential
election
debates"
class="mw-redirect">presidential
debates</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="In_Your_Honor_.282005.E2.80.932006.29"><i>In
Your
Honor</i>
(2005–2006)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
In
Your
Honor
(2005–2006)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Foo_Fighters_Live_29.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Foo_Fighters_Live_29.jpg/220px-Foo_Fighters_Live_29.jpg"
width="220"
height="146"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Foo_Fighters_Live_29.jpg/330px-Foo_Fighters_Live_29.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Foo_Fighters_Live_29.jpg/440px-Foo_Fighters_Live_29.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Foo_Fighters_Live_29.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Foo
Fighters
performing
an
acoustic
show









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Having
spent
a
year
and
a
half
touring
behind
<i>One
by
One</i>,
Grohl
did
not
want
to
rush
into
recording
another
Foo
Fighters
record.
Initially
Grohl
intended
to
write
acoustic
material
by
himself,
but
eventually
the
project
involved
the
entire
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
To
record
its
fifth
album,
the
band
shifted
to
Los
Angeles
and
built
a
recording
studio,
dubbed
Studio
606
West.
Grohl
insisted
that
the
album
be
divided
into
two
discs–one
full
of
rock
songs,
the
other
featuring
acoustic
tracks.<sup
id="cite_ref-Chosen_22-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Chosen-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/In_Your_Honor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
Your
Honor">In
Your
Honor</a></i>
was
released
in
June
2005.
The
album's
singles
included
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Best_of_You_(Foo_Fighters_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
of
You
(Foo
Fighters
song)"
class="mw-redirect">Best
of
You</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/DOA_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DOA
(song)">DOA</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Resolve_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Resolve
(song)">Resolve</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/No_Way_Back/Cold_Day_in_the_Sun?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="No
Way
Back/Cold
Day
in
the
Sun">No
Way
Back/Cold
Day
in
the
Sun</a>&quot;.</p>








<p>During
September
and
October
2005,
the
band
toured
with
<a
href="/wiki/Weezer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Weezer">Weezer</a>
on
what
was
billed
as
the
'<a
href="/wiki/Foozer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Foozer">Foozer</a>
Tour'
as
the
two
bands
co-headlined
the
tour.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
June
17,
2006,
Foo
Fighters
performed
its
largest
non-festival
headlining
concert
to
date
at
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hyde
Park,
London">Hyde
Park</a>.
Mot&ouml;rhead's
<a
href="/wiki/Lemmy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lemmy">Lemmy</a>
joined
the
band
on
stage
to
sing
&quot;Shake
Your
Blood&quot;
from
Dave
Grohl's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Probot_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Probot
(band)"
class="mw-redirect">Probot</a></i>
album.
Also,
as
a
surprise
performance,
<a
href="/wiki/Brian_May?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brian
May">Brian
May</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Meddows-Taylor?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Meddows-Taylor"
class="mw-redirect">Roger
Taylor</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Queen_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Queen
(band)">Queen</a>
jammed
with
Foo
Fighters,
playing
part
of
&quot;We
Will
Rock
You&quot;
as
a
lead
into
&quot;Tie
Your
Mother
Down&quot;.</p>








<p>In
further
support
of
<i>In
Your
Honor</i>,
the
band
decided
to
organize
a
short
acoustic
tour
for
the
summer
of
2006.
The
tour
included
former
member
<a
href="/wiki/Pat_Smear?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pat
Smear">Pat
Smear</a>,
who
rejoined
the
band
as
an
extra
guitarist,
<a
href="/wiki/Petra_Haden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Petra
Haden">Petra
Haden</a>
on
violin
and
backup
vocals,
<a
href="/wiki/Drew_Hester?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drew
Hester">Drew
Hester</a>
on
percussion,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rami_Jaffee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rami
Jaffee">Rami
Jaffee</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Wallflowers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Wallflowers">The
Wallflowers</a>
on
keyboards/piano.
While
much
of
the
setlist
focused
on
<i>In
Your
Honor'</i>s
acoustic
half,
the
band
also
used
the
opportunity
to
play
lesser-known
songs
such
as
&quot;Ain't
It
The
Life&quot;,
&quot;Floaty&quot;,
and
&quot;See
You&quot;.
The
band
also
performed
&quot;Marigold&quot;,
a
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pocketwatch_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pocketwatch
(album)">Pocketwatch</a></i>-era
song
that
was
best
known
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nirvana
(band)">Nirvana</a>
B-side.</p>








<p>In
November
2006,
the
band
released
their
first
ever
live
CD,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Skin_and_Bones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Skin
and
Bones">Skin
and
Bones</a></i>,
featuring
fifteen
performances
captured
over
a
three-night
stint
in
Los
Angeles.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Echoes.2C_Silence.2C_Patience_.26_Grace_and_Greatest_Hits_.282007.E2.80.932009.29"><i>Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace</i>
and
<i>Greatest
Hits</i>
(2007–2009)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace
and
Greatest
Hits
(2007–2009)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Foo_Fighters_Live_21.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""

class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Foo_Fighters_Live_21.jpg/330px-Foo_Fighters_Live_21.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Foo_Fighters_Live_21.jpg/440px-Foo_Fighters_Live_21.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Foo_Fighters_Live_21.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
The
band
performing
live
in
2007









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>For
the
follow-up
to
<i>In
Your
Honor</i>,
the
band
decided
to
call
in
<i>The
Colour
and
the
Shape</i>
producer
Gil
Norton.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Echoes,_Silence,_Patience_%26_Grace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace">Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace</a></i>
was
released
on
September
25,
2007.
The
album's
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Pretender_(Foo_Fighters_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Pretender
(Foo
Fighters
song)">The
Pretender</a>&quot;,
was
issued
to
radio
in
early
August.
In
mid-to-late
2007
&quot;The
Pretender&quot;
topped
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a></i>'s
Modern
Rock
chart
for
a
record
19
weeks.
The
second
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Long_Road_to_Ruin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Long
Road
to
Ruin">Long
Road
to
Ruin</a>&quot;,
was
released
in
December
2007,
supported
by
a
music
video
directed
by
longtime
collaborator
<a
href="/wiki/Jesse_Peretz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jesse
Peretz">Jesse
Peretz</a>
(formerly
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Lemonheads?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Lemonheads">the
Lemonheads</a>).<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
October
2006,
Foo
Fighters
started
its
world
tour
in
support
of
<i>Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace</i>.
The
band
performed
shows
throughout
the
United
States,
Canada,
Europe,
Australia,
New
Zealand
and
Asia,
including
headlining
the
<a
href="/wiki/Virgin_Mobile_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Virgin
Mobile
Festival"
class="mw-redirect">Virgin
Mobile
Festival</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Baltimore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>
on
August
9.
At
the
European
MTV
Music
Awards
in
2007
Pat
Smear
confirmed
his
return
to
the
band.</p>








<p><i>Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace</i>
was
nominated
for
five
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>
in
2008.
Foo
Fighters
went
home
with
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Rock
Album"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Album</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Hard_Rock_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Hard
Rock
Performance"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Hard
Rock
Performance</a>
(for
&quot;The
Pretender&quot;).
The
album
was
also
nominated
for
Album
of
the
Year,
while
&quot;The
Pretender&quot;
was
also
nominated
for
Record
of
the
Year
and
Best
Rock
Song.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Foo_Fighters_with_John_Paul_Jones_and_Jimmy_Page,_2008.jpg"
target="_blank"

Paul
Jones,
Taylor
Hawkins,
Jimmy
Page,

and

1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Foo_Fighters_with_John_Paul_Jones_and_Jimmy_Page%2C_2008.jpg/440px-Foo_Fighters_with_John_Paul_Jones_and_Jimmy_Page%2C_2008.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Foo_Fighters_with_John_Paul_Jones_and_Jimmy_Page,_2008.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"

src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"

/></a>










</div>
Hawkins
(second
from
left)
and
Grohl
(right)
with











<a
href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Paul

(musician)">John

(left)
and











<a
href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimmy

Page</a>
(second
from
right)
of











<a
href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Led
Zeppelin">Led
Zeppelin</a>
performing
at











<a
href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wembley
Stadium">Wembley
Stadium</a>,
London
in
2008









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>On
June
7,
2008,
the
band
played
<a
href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wembley
Stadium">Wembley
Stadium</a>,
London
and
was
joined
by
<a
href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimmy
Page">Jimmy
Page</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Paul
Jones
(musician)">John
Paul
Jones</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Led
Zeppelin">Led
Zeppelin</a>
to
play
&quot;Rock
and
Roll&quot;
(with
Grohl
on
drums
and
Hawkins
on
vocals)
and
&quot;Ramble
On&quot;
(sung
by
Grohl,
drums
by
Hawkins).
As
Page
and
Jones
left
the
stage
before
a
final
encore
of
&quot;Best
Of
You&quot;,
an
ecstatic
Grohl
shouted
&quot;Welcome
to
the
greatest
fucking
day
of
my
whole
entire
life!&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
Throughout
the
tour
for
<i>Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace</i>,
Foo
Fighters
had
been
writing
and
practicing
new
songs
at
sound
checks.
After
Foo
Fighters
had
completed
this
tour
in
September
2008,
they
recorded
13
new
songs
in
studio
606,
shortly
after
announcing
a
hiatus
from
touring
(which
would
last
until
January
2011).
These
sessions
likely
lasted
from
late
2008
-
early
2009.
While
the
members
of
Foo
Fighters
had
initially
planned
for
their
new
album
(composed
of
songs
from
this
recording
session)
to
have
come
out
in
2009
with
almost
no
touring
support,
they
ultimately
decided
to
shelve
most
of
the
songs
from
these
sessions.
Three
of
these
songs
were
later
released
-
&quot;Wheels&quot;
and
&quot;Word
Forward&quot;
(which
were
directly
placed
on
their
greatest
hits
album),
and
a
newly
recorded
version
of
&quot;Rope&quot;
(which
ended
up
making
the
final
cut
of
&quot;Wasting
Light&quot;).<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
November
3,
2009,
the
band
released
a
compilation
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Foo_Fighters_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greatest
Hits
(Foo
Fighters
album)">Greatest
Hits</a></i>,
which
features
two
new
songs,
&quot;Word
Forward&quot;
and
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wheels_(Foo_Fighters_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wheels
(Foo
Fighters
song)">Wheels</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
These
songs
were
recorded
during
a
session
which
occurred
between
&quot;Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
and
Grace&quot;
and
&quot;Wasting
Light&quot;
coming
out.
In
order
to
promote
their
greatest
hits
album,
Foo
Fighters
performed
a
show
at
studio
606
in
October
2009
(which
was
broadcast
online),
during
which
the
band
took
fan
requests.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"

Light</i>
(2010–2012)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Wasting
Light
(2010–2012)">edit</a>]</span></h3>

tright">
