Foo
Fighters
in
2009,
from
left
to
right:
Hawkins,
Shiflett,
Grohl,
Mendel









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>In
August
2010,
the
band
began
recording
their
seventh
studio
album
with
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Butch_Vig?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Butch
Vig">Butch
Vig</a>,
who
had
previously
produced
the
two
new
tracks
for
the
band's
<i>Greatest
Hits</i>
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
recorded
in
Dave
Grohl's
garage
using
only
analog
equipment.
The
album
won
five
Grammys
and
was
nominated
for
six.
Vig
said
in
an
interview
with
MTV
that
the
album
was
entirely
analog
until
post-mastering.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
Pat
Smear
was
present
in
many
photos
posted
by
Grohl
on
Twitter
and
a
press
release
in
December
confirmed
Smear
played
on
every
track
on
the
album
and
was
considered
a
core
member
of
the
band
once
again,
having
initially
left
as
a
full-time
member
in
1997
before
returning
as
a
touring
guitarist
in
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-fooarchive.com_32-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-fooarchive.com-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
first
single
from
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wasting_Light?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wasting
Light">Wasting
Light</a></i>,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Rope_(Foo_Fighters_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rope
(Foo
Fighters
song)"
class="mw-redirect">Rope</a>&quot;,
was
released
to
radio
in
February
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
April
16,
2011,
Foo
Fighters
released
an
album
of
covers,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Medium_Rare_(Foo_Fighters_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Medium
Rare
(Foo
Fighters
album)">Medium
Rare</a></i>,
as
a
limited-edition
vinyl
for
<a
href="/wiki/Record_Store_Day?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Record
Store
Day">Record
Store
Day</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
promotion
for
the
album
has
been
highly
praised
for
its
originality.<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Wasting
Light</i>
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
200
chart,
being
the
first
Foo
Fighters
album
to
do
so.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Alongside
<i>Wasting
Light</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
release,
Foo
Fighters
released
a
rock
documentary,
directed
by
Academy
Award-winner
<a
href="/wiki/James_Moll?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Moll">James
Moll</a>.
The
film,
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Back_and_Forth_(Foo_Fighters_documentary)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Back
and
Forth
(Foo
Fighters
documentary)"
class="mw-redirect">Back
and
Forth</a></i>,
chronicling
the
band's
career—from
the
dissolution
of
Nirvana
due
to
the
death
of
frontman
Kurt
Cobain
to
the
formation
of
Foo
Fighters
as
Dave
Grohl's
&quot;one-man
band&quot;
to
the
status
of
the
band
in
2011.
All
the
current
and
past
bandmembers,
plus
producer
Butch
Vig,
tell
the
story
of
the
band
through
interviews.
After
debuting
on
March
15,
2011
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/SXSW?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="SXSW"
class="mw-redirect">SXSW</a>
festival
in
<a
href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Austin,
Texas">Austin,
Texas</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
it
was
eventually
released
on
DVD
on
June
2011.</p>








<p>On
May
21,
2011,
Foo
Fighters
headlined
the
middle
day
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hangout_Music_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hangout
Music
Festival">Hangout
Music
Festival</a>
in
Gulf
Shores,
Alabama.
On
June
4,
2011,
they
played
a
surprise
set
at
the
2011
<a
href="/wiki/KROQ_Weenie_Roast?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="KROQ
Weenie
Roast">KROQ
Weenie
Roast</a>.
They
also
headlined
two
sold
out
shows
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/National_Bowl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="National
Bowl">Milton
Keynes
National
Bowl</a>
on
July
2
and
3,
supported
by
artists
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Alice_Cooper?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alice
Cooper">Alice
Cooper</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Seasick_Steve?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Seasick
Steve">Seasick
Steve</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Paul
Jones">John
Paul
Jones</a>.
They
headlined
the
final
night
at
the
20th
anniversary
of
<a
href="/wiki/Lollapalooza?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Chicago?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chicago">Chicago's</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Grant_Park_(Chicago)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grant
Park
(Chicago)">Grant
Park</a>
on
August
7,
2011,
performing
part
of
their
set
in
a
driving
rainstorm.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
2011
Foo
Fighters
played
its
final
shows
of
the
year
through
Australia
and
New
Zealand
with
support
from
Tenacious
D,
finishing
at
Western
Springs,
<a
href="/wiki/Auckland_New_Zealand?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Auckland
New
Zealand"
class="mw-redirect">Auckland,
New
Zealand</a>
on
December
13.</p>








<p>On
August
27,
2012,
Foo
Fighters
ended
its
European
tour
with
a
performance
at
<a
href="/wiki/Reading_and_Leeds_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reading
and
Leeds
Festival"
class="mw-redirect">Reading
and
Leeds
Festival</a>.
On
September
21,
2012,
the
band
headlined
the
Music
Midtown
Festival
in
<a
href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Atlanta,
Georgia"
class="mw-redirect">Atlanta,
Georgia</a>.
The
following
evening,
the
band
headlined
the
DeLuna
Festival
in
<a
href="/wiki/Pensacola_Beach,_Florida?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pensacola
Beach,
Florida">Pensacola
Beach,
Florida</a>.
On
September
29,
2012,
the
band
performed
at
the
Global
Citizens'
Festival,
before
embarking
on
a
break.<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Eighth_studio_album_.282013.E2.80.93present.29">Eighth
studio
album
(2013–present)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Eighth
studio
album
(2013–present)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Despite
initially
announcing
a
break
after
supporting
<i>Wasting
Light</i>,
Grohl
later
stated
in
January
2013
that
the
band
had
started
writing
material
for
an
eighth
studio
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
February
20,
2013
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Brit_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brit
Awards">Brit
Awards</a>,
Grohl
said
he
was
flying
back
to
America
the
following
day
to
start
work
on
the
next
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
an
interview
with
<a
href="/wiki/XFM?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="XFM">XFM</a>,
Grohl
announced
that
their
next
album
has
been
slated
for
a
2014
release.
Grohl
said
“Well,
I’ll
tell
you,
we
have
been
in
our
studio
writing
and
in
the
past
few
weeks
we’ve
written
an
album
and
we
are
going
to
make
this
album
in
a
way
that
no-one’s
ever
done
before
and
we’re
pretty
excited
about
it…
It’s
a
little
ways
off
–
it’s
not
ready
to
happen
right
now
–
but
I
think
next
year
is
going
to
be
a
really
big
year
for
the
Foo
Fighters,
without
question.”</p>








<p>On
September
6,
2013,
Shiflett
posted
a
photo
to
his
<a
href="/wiki/Instagram?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Instagram">Instagram</a>
account
that
indicates
13
songs
are
being
recorded
for
the
new
album
and
later
described
the
album
in
an
interview
as
&quot;pretty
fucking
fun&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Rami_Jaffee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rami
Jaffee">Rami
Jaffee</a>
has
recorded
parts
for
three
songs,
one
of
which
is
entitled
&quot;In
The
Way.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Butch_Vig?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Butch
Vig">Butch
Vig</a>,
who
worked
with
the
band
on
<i>Wasting
Light</i>,
confirmed
via
<a
href="/wiki/Twitter?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Twitter">Twitter</a>
in
late
August
2013
that
he
is
producing
the
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band
confirmed
that
it
will
end
its
hiatus
and
play
two
shows
in
<a
href="/wiki/Mexico_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mexico
City">Mexico
City</a>,
Mexico
on
December
11
and
13,
2013.
On
October
31,
2013,
a
video
appeared
on
the
official
Foo
Fighters
YouTube
channel
showing
a
motorcyclist,
later
shown
as
actor
<a
href="/wiki/Erik_Estrada?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Erik
Estrada">Erik
Estrada</a>,
delivering
each
of
the
band
members
an
invitation
to
play
in
Mexico.<sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
January
16,
2014
a
picture
was
posted
to
Foo
Fighters'
Facebook
page
with
several
master
tapes
with
some
labeled
&quot;LP
8.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Other_appearances">Other
appearances</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Other
appearances">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>It
was
announced
on
September
28,
2011,
that
Foo
Fighters
would
be
performing
during
the
closing
ceremony
of
<a
href="/wiki/Blizzard_Entertainment?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blizzard
Entertainment">Blizzard
Entertainment</a>'s
annual
video
game
convention,
<a
href="/wiki/BlizzCon_2011?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BlizzCon
2011"
class="mw-redirect">BlizzCon</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
September
5,
2012,
the
band
performed
a
show
at
the
Fillmore
in
<a
href="/wiki/Charlotte,_NC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Charlotte,
NC"
class="mw-redirect">Charlotte,
NC</a>
as
a
benefit
for
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_The_Vote?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
The
Vote"
class="mw-redirect">Rock
The
Vote</a>.
The
show,
which
occurred
at
the
same
time
that
the
2012
<a
href="/wiki/Democratic_National_Convention?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Democratic
National
Convention">Democratic
National
Convention</a>
was
being
held
in
Charlotte,
NC,
was
announced
only
two
weeks
prior.
All
tickets
to
the
2000
capacity
venue
sold
out
in
under
60
seconds,
setting
a
record
for
the
venue.<sup
id="cite_ref-49"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
set
another
personal
record
during
the
show
itself,
which
was
the
longest
that
the
band
had
played
to
date,
lasting
just
under
3.5
hours
with
a
setlist
consisting
of
36
songs.<sup
id="cite_ref-50"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_style_and_legacy">Musical
style
and
legacy</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"
title="Edit
section:
Musical
style
and
legacy">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>When
Grohl
first
started
the
band,
its
music
was
often
compared
to
that
of
his
previous
group,
Nirvana.
Grohl
acknowledged
that
Nirvana
singer/guitarist
Kurt
Cobain
was
a
major
influence
on
his
songwriting.
Grohl
said,
&quot;Through
Kurt,
I
saw
the
beauty
of
minimalism
and
the
importance
of
music
that's
stripped
down.&quot;
Foo
Fighters
also
utilize
the
technique
of
shifting
between
quiet
verses
and
loud
choruses,
which
Grohl
said
was
influenced
by
the
members
of
Nirvana
&quot;liking
<a
href="/wiki/The_Knack?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Knack">The
Knack</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Bay_City_Rollers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bay
City
Rollers">Bay
City
Rollers</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">Beatles</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/ABBA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ABBA">ABBA</a>
as
much
as
we
liked
<a
href="/wiki/Flipper_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Flipper
(band)">Flipper</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Flag_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Flag
(band)">Black
Flag</a>,
I
suppose&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Foobulous_4-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Foobulous-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Writing
and
recording
songs
for
the
first
Foo
Fighters
album
by
himself,
Grohl
wrote
the
guitar
riffs
to
be
as
rhythmic
as
possible.
He
approached
the
guitar
in
a
similar
manner
to
his
playing
a
drumkit,
assigning
different
drum
parts
to
different
strings
on
the
instrument.
This
allowed
him
to
piece
together
songs
easily;
he
said,
&quot;I
could
hear
the
song
in
my
head
before
it
was
finished.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Alien_parking_5-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Alien_parking-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
Once
Grohl
assembled
a
full
band,
his
bandmates
assisted
in
song
arrangements.<sup
id="cite_ref-Foobulous_4-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Foobulous-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
members
of
Foo
Fighters
meld
melodic
elements
with
heavier
ones.
Grohl
noted
in
1997,
&quot;We
all
love
music,
whether
it's
the
<a
href="/wiki/Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beatles"
class="mw-redirect">Beatles</a>
or
<a
href="/wiki/Queen_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Queen
(band)">Queen</a>
or
<a
href="/wiki/Punk_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Punk
rock">punk
rock</a>.
I
think
the
lure
of
punk
rock
was
the
energy
and
immediacy;
the
need
to
thrash
stuff
around.
But
at
the
same
time,
we're
all
suckers
for
a
beautiful
melody,
you
know?
So
it
is
just
natural.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Foobulous_4-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Foobulous-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Grohl
said
in
2005,
&quot;I
love
being
in
a
rock
band,
but
I
don't
know
if
I
necessarily
wanna
be
in
an
alternative
rock
band
from
the
1990s
for
the
rest
of
my
life.&quot;
Grohl
noted
that
the
band's
acoustic
tour
was
such
an
attempt
to
broaden
the
group's
sound.<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Campaigning_and_activism">Campaigning
and
activism</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Campaigning
and
activism">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Foo
Fighters's
official
website
formerly
linked
to
<a
href="/wiki/Alive_%26_Well_AIDS_Alternatives?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alive
&amp;
Well
AIDS
Alternatives">Alive
&amp;
Well
AIDS
Alternatives</a>,
a
group
led
by
controversial
AIDS
activist
<a
href="/wiki/Christine_Maggiore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christine
Maggiore">Christine
Maggiore</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-52"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
January
2000,
Nate
Mendel
led
a
benefit
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Hollywood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a>
for
the
group
with
a
speech
by
Maggiore
and
free
copies
of
her
book,
<i>What
If
Everything
You
Thought
You
Knew
About
AIDS
Was
Wrong?</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-MJ_53-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MJ-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup>
<sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
full
band
was
shown
in
a
documentary
for
Alive
&amp;
Well
declaring
their
support
before
a
performance.
Links
and
references
to
Alive
&amp;
Well
have
since
been
removed
and
no
further
mentions
or
shows
of
support
have
been
made.</p>








<p>In
September
2011,
before
a
show
in
Kansas
City,
the
band
performed
a
counter-protest
parody
song
in
front
of
a
protest
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Westboro_Baptist_Church?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Westboro
Baptist
Church">Westboro
Baptist
Church</a>.
The
song
mocked
the
church's
opposition
to
homosexuality,
and
was
performed
in
the
same
faux-trucker
garb
that
was
seen
in
the
band's
&quot;Hot
Buns&quot;
promotional
video.<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Awards">Awards</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Foo_Fighters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16"
title="Edit
section:
Awards">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Foo_Fighters?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
awards
and
nominations
received
by
Foo
Fighters">List
of
awards
and
nominations
received
by
Foo
Fighters</a>







</div>








<p><a
href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pitchfork
Media">Pitchfork
Media</a>
described
Grohl
and
the
band
as
&quot;his
generation's
answer
to
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Petty?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Petty">Tom
Petty</a>—a
consistent
hit
machine
pumping
out
working-class
rock.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Pitchfork_57-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Pitchfork-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Foo
Fighters
first
received
a
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>
for
their
music
video
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Learn_to_Fly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Learn
to
Fly">Learn
to
Fly</a>&quot;
in
2000,
and
have
won
ten
others
in
total.
These
include
four
Grammys
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Rock
Album"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Album</a>
category
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/There_Is_Nothing_Left_to_Lose?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="There
Is
Nothing
Left
to
Lose">There
Is
Nothing
Left
to
Lose</a></i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/One_by_One_(Foo_Fighters_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
by
One
(Foo
Fighters
album)">One
by
One</a></i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Echoes,_Silence,_Patience_%26_Grace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace">Echoes,
Silence,
Patience
&amp;
Grace</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wasting_Light?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wasting
Light">Wasting
Light</a></i>,
and
three
awards
for
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Hard_Rock_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Hard
Rock
Performance"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Hard
Rock
Performance</a>
for
the
songs
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/All_My_Life_(Foo_Fighters_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
My
Life
(Foo
Fighters
song)">All
My
Life</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Pretender_(Foo_Fighters_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Pretender
(Foo
Fighters
song)">The
Pretender</a>&quot;
and
&quot;White
Limo&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Grammy_58-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Grammy-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
also
received
three
<a
href="/wiki/Kerrang!_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kerrang!
Awards">Kerrang!
Awards</a>.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(February
2014)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
At
the
<a
href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2011
MTV
Video
Music
Awards">2011
MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>,
the
band
won
Best
Rock
Video
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Walk_(Foo_Fighters_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walk
(Foo
Fighters
song)">Walk</a>&quot;.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(February
2014)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
They
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/Radio_Contraband?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radio
Contraband">Radio
Contraband</a>
&quot;Major
Label
Artist
of
the
Year&quot;
in
2011.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(February
2014)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>








<p>On
February
12,
2012,
the
band
performed
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/54th_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="54th
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">54th
Grammy
Awards</a>
playing
&quot;Walk&quot;
along
with
the
remix
version
of
&quot;Rope&quot;,
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Deadmau5?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deadmau5">deadmau5</a>.
The
band
was
nominated
for
six
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>
including
<a
href="/wiki/Album_of_the_Year_(Grammy)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Album
of
the
Year
(Grammy)"
class="mw-redirect">Album
of
the
Year</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Rock
Performance"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Performance</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Hard_Rock/Metal_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Hard
Rock/Metal
Performance"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Hard
Rock/Metal
Performance</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Rock
Song"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Song</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Rock
Album"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Album</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Long_Form_Music_Video?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Long
Form
Music
Video"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Long
Form
Music
Video</a>
(for
<i><a
href="/wiki/Back_and_Forth_(Foo_Fighters_documentary)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Back
and
Forth
(Foo
Fighters
documentary)"
class="mw-redirect">Back
and
Forth</a></i>).
They
won
five
out
of
the
six,
losing
only
to
<a
href="/wiki/Adele_(singer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Adele
(singer)"
class="mw-redirect">Adele</a>
in
the
Album
of
the
Year
category.<sup
id="cite_ref-59"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<script
type="text/javascript">




render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Foo_Fighters&page=1&ac=24&qid=949B4F7DF46153F2E5A052CC6FC834E2&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

</script>
